<Author>fanofbarcelona
<Content>Just loved it !!! My husband and I booked the Montecarlo on the basis of its ranking on Trip Advisor and we were not disappointed. The hotel turned out to be far more attractive then it appeared on the photos and it was bliss right from the moment that the doorman/security guy nods his discreet welcome. We were given a room overlooking the Ramblas with our own private balcony. It turned out to be incredibly quiet because of the thoughtfully installed double doors. The bathroom was luxury itself, with an enormous jacuzzi (read small swimming pool), bathrobes, slippers and all the modcons you could wish for. The beds were great for resting after a long day because they could be raised to a seating position or to drain your legs. The staff were incredibly polite and friendly. Quique in particular gave us excellent restaurant recommendations and was very welcoming with a wicked sense of humour. The hotel is perfectly located on the Ramblas (we could people watch from our balcony), close to the Plaza de Catalunya and great for nightlife in the Barri Gotic. Barcelona is culture, culture, culture bursting with museums and incredible gothic, modernista and contemporary architecture. Don't miss the MNAC (museum of Catalunyian art) and its wonderful restaurant with a view called Oleum. The hop-on buses are an excellent way to get to all the top cultural sites. It is worth booking a ticket for two days rather than one. Thank you to all the past reviewers of this hotel for pointing us in the direction of the best hotel possible! It really made our holiday!!

<Author>DrMo
<Content>really nice but caution for wheelchair users or toddlers We stayed here with our 1 year old son for the 3 kings parade and christmas markets. Flying from Bournemouth to Girona airport is very simple and the airport bus waits for the flight. A return to the bus station is 24 euros each and is extremely punctual and efficient (on the return as well). It takes 1hr 10 mins into the station. We then picked up a taxi from upstairs which cost 8 euros and took about 10 minutes.We were put in the new wing which is minimally and tastefully decorated. Good points are wheel chair access into the building but the lifts are very small, some of the spaces in the room again are very narrow so difficulties manoevering a wheel chair but the beds are adjustable and there was a closimat toilet if you could get into the bathroom. The breakfast which is 11 euros per person is up some stairs and there is no other access. Great coffee and very freshly squeezed orange juice and a good range of pastries and cold cuts.Why caution for toddlers - huge staircases leading off open corridors - its a long way down! You pay for a cot 10 euros a night but they do have a high chair. No evening meal service or room service or even tea and coffee making facilities and the restaurants on Las Rambas are limited for small kids unless you want fast food. The staff as previously said are all charming and the majority speak very good English. A nice place

<Author>Geoffhailz
<Content>Great hotel in a superb location The Montecarlo is in a fantastic location. Its right on the Ramblas, at the top end, so is convenient for pretty well everything that you could want. If you are getting the bus in from the airport (and thats the best way) then its only a couple of minutes walk from the Plaza Catalunya terminus.We would only add to the recommendations of the hotel, so we wont bother. Its great, and so is the breakfast!.Let me suggest a couple of things to do. Firstly, DO VISIT THE MARKET !. Its only 5 minutes down the Ramblas (towards the harbour, on the right). I have never seen such a fantastic market anywhere. Fruit, fish, veg are all set out in spectacular displays. The prices are lower when you get away from the main way in - but just go to see all the fantastic displays.Also, we really enjoyed a day trip out to Montserrat. Its an easy train trip from Barcelona ( even if there are a lot of stops). The monastery was interesting ( try to get there for the singing at 1pm) but best of all was taking the St Joan funicular up to the top of the mountain, and then walking back (get a leaflet from the information centre). We did route 5 - a bit rough, so wear strong shoes, and it takes a couple of hours ... but stupendous scenery.All in all, the Montecarlo is a really recommended base for a break in Barcelona.

<Content>Didn't break the bank! As ever chose off Tripadvisor and was not disappointed. the location is ace - right on the Ramblas - letting you walk to nearly everything.We had a 'junior suite' at the back on the first floor - great size with a lobby leading to the bathroom and bedroom and then a lounge off the bedroom. <Content>The best hotel in Barcelona! My husband and I came to Barcelona for the tail end of our Spain honeymoon and the Hotel Montecarlo did not disappoint! The deluxe room was SUPER SPACIOUS with adjustable beds!! Hardwood floors throughout, HUGE bathroom with marble floors and a sitting room with a mini bar and flat screen TV. The service is EXCELLENT. <Author>jokero
<Content>Great Location and Terrific Service We booked the Montecarlo after reading all the fabulous reviews on tripadvisor and stayed for 3 nights in Aug. Given all we had read, it is fair to say we had pretty high expectations (and we paid 207 euros a night). Overall I would say it lived up to most of these, but having spent 3 weeks travelling around Spain (and staying in many hotels) I'm not sure it deserves the incredibly high praise it seems to get from most (given it is not cheap).There is no doubt, the location is very handy, although we found La Rambla to be very touristy (and a bit tacky). You can walk to many sights and the metro and bus stops are closeby. The hotel staff were excellent. They were all very friendly and incredibly helpful. We got some recommendations from the hotel manager on the day we left (as we were driving north into the Pyrenees) that was fabulous. He went out of his way to assist and even called a hotel and did some searching on the internet for us. The room was very comfortable and quiet. A minor point, our high tech beds squeaked a bit when we rolled over. The internet access in the room was a little expensive but there is a free computer in the lobby.Breakfast was reasonably priced and tasty. Overall, this is still a good choice, but I'm not entirely sure you get what you pay for.

<Author>Tazmaniac
<Content>MonteCarlo or Bust!! I have just returned from this superb hotel after a 3 day break in Barcelona. I stayed here on the back of reading the reviews and was blown away.Like a previous reviewer, we had the priviledge of staying in 402 with it's electrically controlled beds, useful lounge area, a bathroom larger than some rooms I have stayed in and it's birds-eye view of La Ramblas. On closing the balcony doors, the only noise we heard from the streets below was from a police car driving up the road in the late evening. Even the aircon was quiet (something I rarely find in a hotel room).The staff could not have been more helpful. There was someone waiting at the door to take our luggage, the receptionist gave us a pile of tourist literature to browse through when we checked in and on our last day our luggage was securely looked after following our noon checkout.I will be staying here again on my next trip to Barcelona and have already recommended it to loads of people.TIP: if arriving at Barcelona airport, catch the A1 bus just outside terminal B - cost 4 euro per person instaed of the 40 euro for a taxi.

<Author>MalcNRhona
<Content>Wonderful hotel We booked this hotel based on the excellent reviews already on this site. We were not disappointed at all. In fact our expectations were exceeded.It was our honeymoon, so we booked a deluxe room (402) which had its own small balcony and overlooked La Rambla - so right in the middle of all the action. However, two sets of double glazing meant that we didn't hear a peep from all the noise and bustle. The beds were independent adjustable singles which are pushed together (this is the same in all the rooms) and were incredibly comfortable.We can't praise the staff highly enough. They were so courteous and helpful, with restaurant recommendations and when they found out it was our honeymoon a bottle of cava, a red rose and some chocolates were placed in our room for us when we came back in after a hard day being tourists. The buffet breakfast was also very good with a varied selection and serving up til a civilised 11am!We wouldn't hesitate to go back.

<Author>emmamaria
<Content>Excellent Montecarlo Stayed for 3 nights end of July. Very friendly and helpful staff, very good English spoken.We had a room with balcony overlooking the Rambllas which was well soundproofed. Adjustable beds, jacuzzi bath, very clean.A nice touch was a chocolate sample in the room every night. The Attic restaurant close by recommended by the hotel was very good. Love Barcelona, lots to see and do, magnificent Gaudi architecture but also football, sand and sea. The street artists are fascinating, and the trees and sounds of the Rambllas.

<Content>Excellent all round This is an excellent hotel in an amazing location, right on La Rambla. My initial concern was regarding noise levels from the street below (as some people in Barcelona never seem to go to sleep) but there were two double-glazed sliding doors onto the balcony which completely eliminated all noise (Room 301 - classed as a Standard Room ). It will be top of my list if (and hopefully when) we return to Barcelona.

<Content>Brilliant hotel We stayed at this hotel based on the TripAdvisor reviews and certainly weren't disappointed. It is in a fab location, halfway down La Ramblas but is a calm oasis of marble in the middle of the bustle of LR and close to the Gothis Quarter. Lovely, minimalist rooms - and the beds are SO comfortable with very good quality linens and comfy matresses. <Content>Loved the Montecarlo! We read the reviews on Hotel Montecarlo on Trip Advisor and decided that it looked good. Well, we were not disappointed. This was truly a 5 star hotel experience. Before arriving I emailed the hotel and asked if I could store my bike there while my wife and I traveled throughout Spain. They promply said yes. Upon arriving in the taxi I was met by one of the hotel staff who carried my bike inside ,indicating that he knew I was coming and that I had a bike with me. He reassured me the bike would be stored safely and securely. I was stunned that they remembered and how efficiently they handled the bike and storage.This was how our stay was here the entire time. Each time we departed and arrived we were greeted warmly.The hotel is in a fantastic location. We walked everywhere we needed to go. Food and ambience is great and a very good value.My only criticism of the hotel is the lack of non smoking rooms. The staff deserve high marks. This number one rated trip advisor hotel lived up to its ranking. I highly recommend this hotel for your Barcelona stay. They are number one.

<Author>Orville_2
<Content>Trust the Reviews for this hotel! My wife  I stayed at the Hotel Montecarlo for two nights at the end of June. It is as good as other reviewers have stated (thank you). We were coming off a cruise so we would arrive at the hotel early in the day so I had emailed the hotel ahead of time to confirm they would have a luggage lock-up we could use (they had replied that they did). However, upon our arrival at about 10:00 am, presumably knowing we were arriving early, they informed us that they had our room ready. Impressive service! We got an updated room which was a little plain (art-deco-ish style) compared with many hotels we've stayed at, but very tastefully done. The bathroom was excellent, which is something that you don't always see in Europe. We had no problem with the dual beds making up the king-size bed that other reviewers have mentioned. The staff were great, explaining the various features of the room like the electric blinds, air conditioning and beds and they handed us some useful tourist books without our even asking. The room was clean, quiet and well maintained. What more could you ask for? We had the 11 Euro breakfast one morning, which was ok but about the only thing I would not rate as exceptional.This was our first visit to Barcelona and I was amazed at how good a location this hotel has. Besides being on La Ramblas, it is also near Placa Catalunya which is a transportation hub, if not the hub of the city. The Metro, buses, airport bus and city tour buses are just a couple of minutes walk from the hotel. When we sadly left, we took the airport bus from there which only costs 4 Euros and 5 cents each. Overall, this hotel deserves its high rating.

<Author>Lutecia
<Content>I will go back to this hotel for all future Barcelona trips I agree to all other good reviews on this hotel. It is excellent.I normally avoid going back to the same hotel so I could try new places, however, this is one of a few places I would actually go back as my regular hotel in this city.The rooms are stylished decorated, yet very functional.Housekeeping standard is very high.The location is simply fantastically convenient to go anywhere. The staff are extremely helpful and friendly.Only two negatives, if I am to raise:1. As one of of the previous reviewers commented, King sized bed is actually made of two single beds, which obviously is not ideal.2. This is probabaly only summer time but just in case some travellers may not like it - The hotel shares its courtyard area with the next door hotel which has a open air restaurant/cafe there. From about 21:00, they have open air cinema, which is quite loud and if your room faces this side (which itself is a good thing as it is quieter than facing La Rambla) you will hear it even with your window closed. It finishes around 23:00 so, if you are out for dinner for these hours, it should not cause you a headache. Also, if you leave your window open overnight, you will be woken up by the strong smell of breakfast preparation from this restaurant in the morning. You may wish to shut the window and leave AC on if you would rather avoid this.

<Author>TwoDRs
<Content>Exceptional in Barcelona (or anywhere!) We stayed at the Hotel Montecarlo for one night following our Mediterranean cruise. Chose this property based on the reviews on this site, backed up by other good recommendations in Frommers and Fodors. We were not disappointed. The room itself was very high end, in line with any top boutique hotel in the United States. The staff was exceptionally willing to help with maps, restaurant recommendations and transportation. They all speak English to some extent, and if the particular individual didn't, there was always someone there they could ask.Wireless Internet was free, and there is also Internet via television available in the room. Two HD televisions with various channels available, very upscale bathroom with whirlpool tub and multi-head shower, full-size hair dryer and toiletries, also a mini refrigerator. Our superior double had a view of the peaceful inner courtyard. There was no noise from the street.The location can't be beat in the center of the La Rambla district, near the Boqueria market and adjoining the Barri Gotic (easy walk behind the property). Two blocks from Plaza Catalunya, where our bus dropped us off after the cruise, so we did need to drag our luggage that distance to the hotel (buses can't drive up La Rambla). This was not a problem, it seems to be the accepted way to do it there. We had been told that no cars could drive up to the hotel, but there is a street out front and taxis can pull up out front.Although we did the final booking through our travel agent, we had already contacted the Hotel Montecarlo directly via email to get quotes and inquire about the hotel and Barcelona in general. They were most helpful and responded right away to every request. Our travel agent was planning to book a different hotel for our small group and we insisted on the Montecarlo.There is a nice breakfast room with eggs, cereals, lots of fruit, bread and pastries, however the breakfast is 11 euros additional per person, a small negative in my book. However, it was very convenient the next morning as we were hurrying to leave for the airport.The only other negative is that the bed, although comfortable, was two individual beds pushed together and they tended to separate - something to consider if you want to cuddle. :-)Otherwise, it was a great way to end our wonderful vacation. Do not hesitate to choose the Montecarlo!!  
<Date>Jun 10, 2008

<Author>Roadrunner15
<Content>MonteCarlo lives up to its great reviews We spent 4 nights (Post Cruise) at the MonteCarlo and loved the hotel. Our room (202) was one of the refurbished rooms. (Staff told us the second and fifth floors had been redone.) The room was large, had a sitting room, a small balcony overlooking Las Ramblas and a large bath. It had new wood floors, quality contemporary furnishings, adjustable bed (fun to sit up and read or watch TV at night), in-room safe, mini-bar, nice closet with storage shelves, a shelf for luggage, two flat screen TVs, nice quality linens and pillows, two bed lights for reading, etc. The sitting room had a wonderful bay window overlooking Las Ramblas.  Watching the action on the street is great fun. The noise is NOT an issue since the hotel has used electric rolling shutters, double sets of doors and a heavy door between the sitting room and bedroom to block the sound. We slept great.The bath had high end decor and fixtures - interesting stone counters, walls and surrounds, high-end Grohe fixtures, whirlpool tub, shower, bidet, toilet, a good hair dryer, bath scales and the usual nice toiletries. Everything you could want was provided.The staff speaks English and are outstanding. They willingly make restaurant reservations, provide help with transportation, maps, and other info. The housekeeping is very quiet and out of sight but excellent. The room was immaculate always. They never knocked on our door and distrubed us to clean. They simply always came while we were gone.We frequently used the free computer with internet in the lobby and took advantage of the breakfast buffet ($11 euros). We appreciated that it stayed open until 11 a.m. and 11:30 a.m. on weekends.We plan to go again to the MonteCarlo. It is very user-friendly and a great place to stay. It could not be in a more convenient location for everything (metro, bus, taxis, tourist sights, restaurants, grocery store, fun and action), and the staff and service are terrific.

<Content>Perfect stay! Stayed at the Montecarlo for 3 nights and was extremely pleased.The hotel's location is perfect. It is on the Rambla near Plaza Catalunya, so very near to starting point of airport bus and tourist hop on hop off and located in the Barri Gotico, in short the heart of the city. You can walk to many important sights, and don't need a taxi or metro. The staff are very friendly and extremely helpful, and speak perfect english.Roger, the porter, who found that the allocated room smelled of smoke, came back to give us an even nicer room.Room 306, their standard room, but perfect. <Author>joeh76
<Content>Absolutely loved the Montecarlo We stayed in the Montecarlo for 4 nights in early January this year and were very impressed. We booked one of the deluxe rooms and really believe it was well worth the extra money. First of all the room and the en-suite were huge. The bathroom was easily the biggest we've had and having the jacuzzi bath and seperate walk-in showers after a long day spent sightseeing was a godsend. The bed itself was one of the most comfortable beds I've stayed in. Entertainemnt wise we had a full minibar, mini hifi system and multichannel tv. What was really cool is that the hifi was wired into the bathroom so you could relax in the bath sipping some chilled cava while listing to your favourite tunes. Total bliss. We didnt sample breakfast as we booked room only, however there are plenty of nice places nearby which do lovely reasonably priced meals.All the staff we met during our stay were incredibly helpful. The gave us tips on what to see and do and they were only too happy to book restaurants and taxis. The hotels location is very central, literally 5 mins walk from La Catalunya railway station. However travelling from the airport its not advisable to take the metro, its best to take the bus to Placa Catalunya and walk 5 mins to the hotel. I would definitely recommend the Montecarlo to anyone going to Barcelona and will stay there again next time I go to Barcelona.

<Author>DevaEboracum
<Content>Perfect Hotel My girlfriend and I stayed here for a short break of four nights in February 2008, and I have to say that the hotel was perfect in every respect - I don't think I could find a thing to fault it.I selected this hotel after reading reviews on Trip Advisor and after looking at all the top rated hotels for both a central location and price, this seemed to be the perfect combination.We arrived early Friday evening and found the hotel located in a perfect spot on La Rambla just a couple of minutes from Place Catulunya.We were greeted at the door by a hotel porter (although I don't believe he was there all the time during the stay, so it may just be pot luck on whether there is a porter there when you arrive). The porter took our bags to reception where we were swiftly and efficiently checked in by a polite and helpfull receptionist with perfect English.After checking in, the porter went with us to the room, carrying the bags and then showing us the features etc. of the room.The room was great - a good sized room with king size bed, contemporary style and nice and clean. The room had doors which opened to overlook La Rambla - and even though the street outside was busy and bustling, you could close the doors and all was quiet. In fact, the hotel was quiet as a whole - everyday we had a nice long lie in without being woken up by noise. The bathroom was wonderful - a good size, clean and with a nice big jacuzzi - big enough for two :-)) with a good shower over the bath.TV was limited in choice - only BBC World and CNN in English - but we didn't go to Barcelona to watch TV. Reception had free Internet access.Overall this was an excellent hotel that I would definitely recommend.TIP - the tax from the airport to the hotel was about 40 Euros inc. tip. However, the Airport bus stops and starts in Placa Catulunya and is five mins walk to the hotel straight down La Rambla. The airport bus only cost 4 Euros per person.

<Author>ghacker0
<Content>Wonderful hotel, friendly with very nice rooms and superbly located We have just come back from a three night stay in Barcelona and stayed at the Montecarlo. When we visited the city 7 years ago, my husband fell in love with the outside of the building and vowed he would stay there if he ever went again. For his birthday, I booked this short break and he was delighted that I had managed to book a room there. Despite only having a standard room, when I spoke to the hotel, they said they would do their best to let us have a balcony. When we arrived they confirmed that we did indeed have a balcony overlooking La Rambla. The room, whilst not being the biggest we have stayed in was very good, and the bathroom was magnificent with a huge jacuzzi bath big enough for two. The beds were very comfortable with the usual egyptian cotton sheets you would expect in a good quality hotel - even the pillows were to my taste. A novelty was the electric bed, enabling you to sit up and have a drink whilst watching the tv. Although they had Sat TV, the only english channels were CNN and BBC World, however we probably spent more time either walking round the city, or chilling out in the bath to help our aching muscles. The staff were extremely friendly and very helpful. All in all, if we went back to that wonderful city, we would always ask for room 301 at the Montecarlo! If you want a good meal, try El Burrito y Yo in the old quarter. Great food and good ambiance.

<Author>freetogoConnecticut
<Content>First-rate in every way We could not have been happier with the hotel. The location is great, right on La Rembla, two blocks from the Plaza de Catalunya. La Rembla is a main street leading up from the port to the center of the city. It has a wide median strip with lots of kiosks, street entertainers, etc. On Sunday it is particularly crowded because the city's people walk up and down the street and a modern version of a paseo. The site is also convenient for catching the open top-deck tourist buses around town. The two main routes stop right at the plaza. There are also many restaurants, etc. around. There is a small supermarket across the street. The hotel is also near to the subway, and many taxis go by for easy flagging.We took in a flamenco show, and it was almost directly across the street from the hotel. The hotel itself was first-rate, specially for the price (149 euros). The room and bathroom were both quite large and very clean. The room had ad dual-control electric adjustable bed-something I've never seen in a hotel. The bath an a good size whirlpool tub. The staff was quite helpful about booking tickets, restaurant suggestions. The buffet breakfast as extra, but at 9 euros was a good bargain. There is free internet in the lobby.

<Author>blooney
<Content>Quiet and Comfortable Stay We enjoyed our stay at this hotel. Our taxi drove us right up to the door and someone was out immediately to take our bags in and hold them for the day until our room was ready. We had just the standard room on the fifth floor. It was overlooking the courtyard. It was fine with us that it did not overlook La Rambla. I took a nice jacuzzi to unwind after our long flight and it was wonderful. They provided a very nice assortment of perfumes and bath crystals and goodies. Very nice touch. The beds were nice, except that they separated during the night and I ended up sleeping in between the two mattresses because I was too tired w/ jet lag to get out of it!! The only thing I would say negatively about the room is that though it did have a CD player I was surprised at the quality of it. I don't think I would advertise that. But, it was nice to have in the room.The staff was willing to help and if you asked a question, they quickly pulled out a map to show you.The ATM right outside the Hotel is archaic and we were afraid it was going to take our card. We had no problems w/ pickpocketing, although we could sort of spot them in the Boqueria when we were sittiing on bar stools looking at our pockets. Keep your bag in your lap and across your body ALL THE TIME. We absoluteley loved Barcelona and almost wished we were not going on our cruise to stay there longer. Don't miss Boqueria and Pintoxto Bar!!!!We ate and drank like the locals and they liked us for it! (wine at 9 a.m.!) Also go have lunch at 4 CATS!!!!!! Awesome!

<Author>KelpFighter
<Content>Wonderful Start After spending around 20 straight hours on airplanes and in airports, my wife and I arrived at the Montecarlo at 11PM, for the start of a long awaited and eagerly anticipated Spain vacation. I was thinking nap time, but as anyone who has been to Barcelona knows, the city is just waking up about then. So we threw some cold water on our faces and out into the night we went. Barcelona is an exciting and fun city. The Hotel Montecarlo is perfectly situated on Ramblas, a short walk to many fine restaurants and cafes, along with open air markets and museums. For longer jaunts, we took public transportation. Being an urban planner, I truly appreciated Barcelona's splendid combination of art, design, form and function. At no time did I ever feel lost or unsafe (using some common sense, of course). The Hotel Montecarlo was the perfect compliment to our Barcelona experience. The room, overlooking the Ramblas was spacious and modern with a classy shower/jacuzzi tub. The staff was very accommodating and helpful. In particular, we left our passports in our room's safe when we left for Girona. Marina, the front desk staff person, was very helpful and made sure that we received them without incident a few days later. Marina also was extremely helpful regarding local sites, customs and eateries. It was the perfect start to a wonderful vacation. Without a doubt, we would return to the Hotel Montecarlo.

<Author>ninwall
<Content>The Best Hotel I Have Ever Stayed In We just got back from a wonderful week in Barcelona. I booked the Hotel Montecarlo because of the good reviews on TripAdvisor.com, and all I can say is, the hotel was FANTASTIC. We are a family of 4 and booked 2 adjoining rooms on the 5th floor, away from La Rambla. The hotel exceeded our expectations. Our next visit to Barcelona will DEFINITELY include a return to the Hotel Montecarlo.

<Author>BookWriter2
<Content>Lovely, quiet hotel in the middle of everything The Montecarlo was fabulous! This was our first trip to Barcelona and we wanted a location that was central to the touristic sites. When we first walked down La Rambla to the hotel, we were apprehensive because La Rambla was SO packed with people and full of activity - we were worried that it would go on all night and that our room would be noisy. We asked for a quiet room and got 206, which turned out to be in the new part of the hotel on a private courtyard (private to other buildings). Even though we kept the window the the courtyard open every night, we slept in complete silence and tranquility. That was the first thing we loved about the hotel: being in the middle of everything and having it be quiet at night.Besides that: the hotel is stunning. It is a beautiful old (Beaux Arts?) building that has been updated with modern design giving it the best of both worlds. We did not see rooms in the old part, but ours, in the new part was simple and lovely. It had a platform bed, a built-in desk with a free internet line, an ample closet, a chair and small table, and a spacious bathroom. In fact, the bathroom was really gorgeous, with chocolate brown slate tiles, a jacuzzi tub, and modern fixtures. The pictures on the website do not do this hotel justice. It is much prettier!On the mezzanine is a beautiful old sitting room with a magnificent fireplace and lots of sitting areas. It has chairs where you can sit and watch all of the activity on the street.The people working at the hotel were extremely helpful and courteous. The hotel is just two blocks from the Plaza Catalunya, which is where the fabulous touristic buses board and where the airport bus stops. Thus, you can get to the hotel from the airport for only 4 Euros (30 minute trip). Every day that we were at the Montecarlo, my husband said to me Thanks for finding such a great hotel!

<Author>LiverpoolChuckles
<Content>AbsolutelyLoved Hotel Montecarlo My best friend and I stayed at the Hotel Montecarlo on Las Ramblas for 5 nights in September and absolutely loved it! Its at the top end of Las Ramblas close to Placa Catalunya Square (2 min walk) - which made it perfect for catching the Tourist Bus and bus to and from the airport.The hotel is one of, if not the most, beautiful building on las ramblas - loads of tourists took pictures of the building. The staff are incredibly helpful and very friendly. We arrived early and the team gave us a welcome pack full of things to do in Barcelona and looked after our luggage whilst we went and grabbed a bite to eat while our room was getting ready. When we got back our luggage was already in our room, complete with a welcome pack (gorgeous chocolate key, lovely welcome note and gorgeous goodie box). (Top tip though, don't struggle up the steps with your suitcase on arrival - if you go in to the reception desk theres a lift that will take your cases up to the ground floor reception room).We'd asked for a room overlooking Las Ramblas in our email reservation and got one - definitely worth asking. Gorgeous iron balconies, but these do tend to be shared with the next room, but are sectioned off. Once the sliding doors are closed you wouldn't know you were staying on Las Ramblas it was so quiet.The mini bar is restocked often - and is as cheap as anything around the hotel with a good choice of drink for both pre-night and morning after thirst requirements!!. There's a cd player and tv. The beds were remote controlled so you could raise the top or bottom end of the bed to suit. The shower was amazing - a whole room of its own, with a huge jacuzzi bath. There were also complimentary bath robes and slippers (not all out luxury, more of a day spa robe - but a really nice touch).Also - do make the effort to pop up to the roof terrace as the view over the city is lovely.Initially we were considering staying at the 1989 (if thats the right name) which is situated just opposite the Montecarlo. Yes the hotel has a lovely pool at the top, but you really wouldn't miss it. The Montecarlo has a much more relaxed and friendly feel - I can't recommend this enough!

<Author>aptbroker1
<Content>Best Hotel in Barcelona? Yep! After checking on hotels at Tripadvisor, we picked the Hotel Monte Carlo, staying 3 days from 2-5 October. We booked a deluxe room (#402) for 270 Euros through Venere.com at the last minute. We were shocked and amazed by our room! The bathroom alone was bigger than most of our hotel rooms in Europe, all redone in marble with jacuzzi, separate shower, exercise bike and lots of windows providing mellow light. We had a living room with WiFi and cable TV, and the bedroom was palatial, with an adjustable bed that raised both head and/or feet, with a balcony overlooking Las Ramblas, the best location in Barcelona! The entire staff was super friendly and helpful, and the public areas magnificent. Oh, and the breakfast buffet was the best we've had in Europe; eggs, ham, 5 kinds of sausage, 5 or 6 kinds of bread, with a toaster that actually worked! Plus FRESH squeezed orange juice! Heavenly! A word of caution, the regular rooms cannot be this nice, as they are $70 less money, so if you can spring for the extra $$ it's sooo worth it. We felt like the Duke  Duchess of Windsor!

<Author>hamilton44
<Content>An excellent hotel We stayed at the Monte Carlo for 2 nights post-cruise and couldn't have been happier with our choice.The hotel has a baroque appearance from the outside (very lovely when illuminated at night) but it's very modern inside. From the moment our taxi pulled up at the door the staff couldn't have been more helpful (and we did have a lot of bags).We had a quiet room at the back of the hotel - furnished in very modern style and with jacuzzi bath (lovely after our cramped shower on the Emerald Princess). Bathrobes were supplied but we didn't use them. One little complaint...the bath was rather slippery and we would have welcomed a bath mat when showering. The hotel is ideally situated right on La Rambla and very near Catalunya Place and a very central spot e.g. for catching the turistic bus which circumnavigates all the main attractions in the city - both routes, north and south are highly recommended. The staff were very helpful in suggesting good eating places...great recommendations for tapas. We ate breakfast both mornings ( 9 euros per person and well worth it). We would certainly stay at the Monte Carlo again.

<Content>Lives up to the hype!! My wife and I booked the Hotel Montecarlo for the Barcelona stretch of our honeymoon. We booked it based on reviews from this website. We were a little nervous because the hotel is not found on very many travel sites. Bottom line: the entire experience was unforgettable - because of the room, the staff, the location and the price. I had written in advance to advise that it was our honeymoon, and they certainly stepped up to the occasion. They placed us in what they referred to as their newest and best suite. 2nd Floor with a private terrace overlooking La Rambla. seperate bedroom and sitting room. Beautiful decor, cozy kingsize bed, and the greatest bathroom you could imagine with a 2 person jacuzzi, huge seperate shower with rainfall, regular detachable showerhead and horizontal hydrotherapy jets! Double-sink vanity, etc, etc. Moments after the staff checked us in and brought up our bags, the hotel manager arrived with a complementary bottle of cava (spanish champagned) and flowers to congratulate us on the occasion. After each long, wonderful day we would sit out on our terrace with a bottle of cava and watch the excitment of La Rambla go by. Then, the moment we closed the well-soundproofed doors lowered the professionally installed black-out blinds, we were in our private villa which could have been miles from any other people. Seriously folks - This hotel was the highlight of our trip.

<Author>4TUNES
<Content>First Class weekend at the Monte!! Just returned from a wonderful weekend at the Montecarlo Hotel, located directly on Las Ramblas. We paid the extra for a deluxe room...well worth it. On arrival we were given a choice of Ramblas or rear facing rooms. No competition really, we chose room 308 at the rear of the hotel...features a huge jacuzzi, walk in wet room shower with hydro massage, a seating area, 2 tv`s, Hifi, electric beds and blinds and silent air con. Only areas for improvement were no iron in room or tea / coffee facilities. Comprehensive buffet breakfast...well worth the extra.Take the Aerobus from the airport....stops 100 yds from the hotel.By far the best eatery visited was Los Caracoles [-----]....steak, snails and chicken were all the best ever! Visit during the afternoon to take in the local clientele and traditional atmoshere.Las Ramblas is awesome...no problems with pickpockets, but wear your bag in front, not on your back! Brilliant street artists. The place really comes alive at 1.00 a.mThe 2 day tourist bus pass is great value, and covers all the main sites. An added feature being that you dont have to drive and can therefore drink at numerous local bars en route! Gaudi`s Sagrada Familia is without doubt the most awesome structure in Europe. Enjoy!

<Author>Zenawio
<Content>Fantastic all round! Fantastic location - 5 minute walk from the Aerobus (From the airport) stop in Plaza Catalunya. Great staff - Perfect English, plus helpful, friendly and always polite. Right in the middle of everything - On La Rambla, a walk to the beach, a short walk to the Gothic Quarter, a good walk to Sagrada Familia. Great room - Clean, massively comfortable beds, lovely welcome pack, plus a Jacuzzi in the bathroom!!! It was a fantastic place! The breakfast was a little pricey at 9 Euros each, but very, very good....buffet, with a selection of cold and cooked meats, fruit a range of breads and lovely, freshly squeezed orange juice. All in all, it was close to everything - whether that be restaurants, famous sites, bus stops, the beach, culture - way more than a 3 star and for the centre of such a great city as Barcelona, fairly priced.....everything was great! I cannot recommend it enough! One thing to remember is that when you book on your respective websites (I went with Opodo), it didn't detail the 7% Service/VAT Charge......took me by surprise, but it was no fault of the hotel, just something I forgot to take in to account! But, if you go, you will not be disappointed!

<Content>Good location, clean and comfortable. You wont be disappointed Booked a 4 night stay here in August on the back of the tripadvisor reviews and wasn't dissapointed. <Author>DTommo
<Content>Fantastic hotel in ideal location This 3* hotel is definately under-rated. This should at least be given 4*. The hotel is fantastic. The rooms are boutique size with a jacuzzi bathroom of 5* status. Prior to arrival, informed hotel that three day break was in fact a birthday surprise. To this end, a bottle of chilled champagne was awaiting our arrival in the room. Our room, on the 4th floor, had a balcony looking over La Rambla. This view could only be bettered by the view from the hotels 6th floor sun terrace. The staff, especially those on reception, are friendly, helpful and knowledgeable. Breakfast was good...both continental and hot available. Fresh orange juice and coffee served directly to your table. The location of the hotel is indeed first class, almost in the centre of La Rambla, with the main square to the right and the port area to the left. All main points of interest within walking distance of the hotel.Just a few traveller tips:Taxi from airport to hotel door 20 euros. Hotel door to airport 30 euros! Be sure to get price prior to leaving hotel.A pint of beer in La Rambla 9 euros. Just round the corner, price drops to 4 euros.Beware conmen with the 'ball under the three matchboxes' routine. They work in a group to produce their own crowd, enticing 'lucky' tourists!

<Author>holidayprincess
<Content>A Grand Delight Each to their own of course but happily for us our experience couldn't be further removed from a recent review 'a grand disappointment' - it was for us 'a grand delight'. I am an extremely fussy traveller as regards cleanliness, comfort, and luxury, and checked in early and wearily (having been in another hotel in town working at said convention). The room we had requested, balcony overlooking Las Ramblas was unavailable so we were offered an upgrade to their junior suite (104) which more than made up for it. Magnificient - enormous, lots of marble, chandeliers, beautiful furniture, even a small library, and a massage jet shower/sauna, as well as the rugby team sized jacuzzi.Another recent review points out all rooms above 3rd floor are yet to be refurbished, and this was still the case, so we were pleased to be on the 1st floor. No disturbance from the workmen during the week until about 10am by which time we were out or on our way out., and then only light tapping. The staff were unfailingly helpful and chirpy, and made some great restaurant recommendations and reservations for us - even getting us a table on a terrace overlooking the fiesta fireworks on the beach with an hour's notice - impressive! Nice finishing touches like coming in late at night to see tea light candles lit all around the flowers in the lobby, chilling our wine for us, and even lending us their corkscrew. On arriving home there was an e-mail waiting for us to say my husband's mobile had been left in the room (oops), and it arrived here in the UK 3 days later, impressed us further. I believe if you make sure to ask for a refurbed room, you won't stay in a better hotel in Barcelona for the price.

<Content>A grand disappointment We visited the hotel from June 11-14, 2007. We were very disappointed with the quality of this hotel. We booked it based upon the reviews on this site. If you're looking for a nice, clean hotel, this is not the one for you!

<Author>melbguy
<Content>it depends... I loved this hotel when I stayed here a year ago with my partner. I thought it was one of the best hotels I've ever stayed in, and the price was excellent for Barcelona, the quality of the place, and the location. Now I'm not so sure anymore.I was on the third floor, and the renovations on the second were infernally noisy. Yes, they said they'd stop if it bothered me but surely they wouldn't suspend everything for the 5 days I stayed here. Not a big deal if you're out during the day (the work goes from 9 to 6) but if you're planning to spend quality time inside, not pleasant.Last time we had a room with a view of the Ramblas, which was great and quiet. This time, I had a room with no view whatsoever, only looking across a narrow space at another room, and as an earlier reviewer said, there's very little natural light because the top is covered. This made the room very dark and depressing. I would certainly not want to stay in this kind of room again. It may be that this is only the case for single rooms though, so if you're travelling with a companion, it may not be a problem.The third issue is the one that bothered me the most, and probably means that I will never stay here again. When I wanted to bring a friend, who was staying at another hotel, up to my room so he could check his email, the reception desk staff told me I was not allowed to have visitors. He said the little slip you sign at check-in said so on the back. I went up and checked (with my friend waiting downstairs), and indeed, it said that for security, no visitors were allowed. Many hotels have a similar policy, except it's usually something along the lines of visitors must be accompanied by guests at all times. I find it completely unacceptable that a hotel would forbid its guests to have visitors, not to mention very embarrassing for the guest who has to make his visitor wait downstairs. But again, whether this is a problem, depends: if you're not going to have visitors, you won't be bothered by this unfriendly policy.Of course, the hotel still has many positive features. The rooms are nice, the breakfast is actually good value at 9 Euros, and most of the people at the reception desk are very friendly and helpful.So altogether, Hotel Montecarlo is a mixed bag and I can certainly no longer recommend it without reservations.  
<Date>Jun 8, 2007

<Author>Diptych
<Content>Convenient and Friendly There have been many positive reviews of this hotel so my purpose in adding to their number is simply to contribute a couple of topical points.Firstly, we would agree with everything favourable written about the hotel. We had a great stay.Secondly, there has been some renovation taking place in the hotel. During our stay the second floor was sealed off in its entirety. That said ,we were not at all inconvenienced and there was no early morning chorus of hammering nor clouds of dust to contend with.Thirdly, what friendly staff! Genuinely eager to please, helpful and informative.Finally...before our short trip I was worried because the hotel's name did not appear amongst the recommended hotels in the guidebooks we had brought with us - Rough Guide and Dorling Kindersley. I cannot understand why this should be - unless the other hotels in town are of such matchless quality that the Montecarlo pales in comparison. I don't think so.Be guided by the positive reviews found on Trip Advisor and stay at The Montecarlo when in Barcelona. Clean, friendly, convenient and with breakfasts to die for.

<Author>atty_busnss_travlr
<Content>professional staff, quality hotel We spent 4 nights here in late May, third floor front room on the Ramblas. At the time of the stay the third floor had already been renovated, the second was in the midst of renovation, and then they will renovate the 4th and 5th floors. The first floor has a large conference or public room but no guest rooms. I note that the previous reviewer was required to sign a form stating that he understood renovation was ongoing. On the other hand, we were told that if the work bothered us they would immediately stop all work on the room below us. We were always out of the hotel during the day, so it wasn't a problem, but since renovation is likely to be ongoing for months, I recommend people try to stay on renovated floors away from the ongoing work.I did not see inside any rooms on non-renovated floors, but I walked down the hall way on the fifth floor to reach the solarium, and the carpet was very warn. If this is an example of what the rooms themselves look like on the non-renovated floors, I would again recommend keeping with the renovated rooms.We were a little nervous about possible noise in a room directly above the Ramblas, so asked to see a variety of rooms. I have never in my life had hotel staff so willing to show us so many rooms, all on the 3rd floor. I would say the footprint of the rooms were all about the same square footage, large for a European 4 star hotel, and very large for Barcelona. The main difference is the size of the Jacuzzi, and thus the bathroom. The room we ended up accepting, on the Ramblas (and with double doors, each double paned, noise from the Ramblas is a non-issue), had a vast Jacuzzi, and thus probably a third of the room consisted of the bathroom. Another room we were shown had a bathtub that was so small I couldn't possibly see how to get in, or more importantly, out of it. As a result the bathroom was small and the bedroom thus much larger than the bedroom portion of our room. Why in such a huge room would you have a half-bath tub? Weird. And weird also was our swimming pool of a Jacuzzi. It took an immense amount of water to half-fill the thing, and there was a long, and I mean long, set of instructions explaining how to work the thing. Despite both of us reading the instructions out loud to the other, we couldn't get it to work, and when someone arrived to explain it they couldn't get it to work either. Not a problem, but a tad odd. Also odd was the selection of furnishings which ranged from typical 4 star hotel nice wood head board and side board to a lamp that even Ikea would have found cheap which you turned on by yanking the electrical cord!But these are nits. The temperature controls, window coverings and lighting allowed one complete control over the environment, and housekeeping did a very professional job throughout our stay. The room included a table with nice chairs, plenty of reading lights and even a pocket door that you could close in the hallway between the bathroom and bedroom where you could read without disturbing someone sleeping. There is one computer with not very good free internet access in the lobby and a fair selection of international papers. The common seating area is comfortable though rather corporate. I found the solarium rather odd, since it is just an unfinished portion of the roof with an outdoor shower, and the hours are oddly short, 11:00 AM to 7:00 PM.But the area where this hotel really stood out was the professionalism of the staff. Our demands were limited to seeing endless room at check in, having our boarding passes printed the night before we left, borrowing umbrellas, getting wine bottles opened and chilled and receiving explanations of how to reach a couple of destinations. They handled all of these requests very well, and each time we returned to the hotel they remembered our room number. But what really impressed me was the unbelievable range of requests guests threw at them during our stay. A problem back at the office continued to plague my trip, so I spent way too long at that one computer off the lobby. One simply awful young woman demanded that staff find her a rental car to get to her next destination, some resort a couple of hours away. Loudly announcing in her US english that money was not a concern, merely that they find an agency to deliver the car to her and that would allow her to drop the car at the resort. Cheerfully the front desk wrote down this request and began making calls. Hours later when I again sat myself in front of the computer and the woman returned from her day shopping in Barcelona (huge number of expensive bags in tow) and asked about the arrangements, they were able to assure her that the car would arrive the next morning at the requested time, she merely needed to provide her credit card for the reservation. Upon hearing the price ($275 for a 2 or 3 day car rental) she told them to cancel it, it was way above her budget, and instead get her train reservations. I would have hit her (which is one reason why I'm a lawyer and not in the hospitality industry), but they were as pleasant and professional as could be. Another woman was in tears as I sat at the terminal while the desk explained that they had no reservation under her name and the hotel was full for the night. She then admitted that she had never actually received a confirmation from the hotel, but that since she had sent an email and they hadn't actually said no, she assumed...They couldn't have been nicer. They asked her 20 questions about exactly what she wanted in a hotel, what price she was willing to pay  then called and found her a room. They then called her a cab! It got so that every time I returned to the hotel room from my awful battles at the computer trying to solve the office problems I would have at least one story of the incredible people at the front desk. If only they could have solved my office problems with the same smile  attention to detail they afforded each and every request that came past the front desk!

<Author>RodW
<Content>Excellent Hotel We stayed at the MonteCarlo Hotel for two nights May 2  3.We have stayed at numerous hotels throughout the world and I must say this was one of the most enjoyable at any price. The decor of the rooms was great, we had a balcony room overlooking La Ramblas which had double glazed windows and heavy curtains so it was silent and dark if you wanted to sleep. In addition we had a separate sitting area with TV and a fantastic usuable bathroom with spa bath. The location of this hotel is ideal for a first time traveller to Barcelona, but what impressed me most was the attention and commitment of the staff to ensure we enjoyed our stay. The breakfast was great value for money at a cost of 9 euros each (i think).We would not hesiate to stay here again and highly recommend this as a hotel of great value for money. It is certainly not 5 start in it's facilities, but it is for service and experience. Don't forget a visit to the roof top terrace where the views are breathtaking and all over Barcelona.If you judge your hotels on pure value, this is it!! I would prefer this hotel to most 5 star hotels I've stayed at.

<Author>louford
<Content>Loved it!! We stayed at the Montecarlo for three nights. We booked directly through the Hotel's website and got a fantastic room with a balcony overlooking Las Ramblas. With the double double-glazed doors closed, almost all street noise was removed so light sleepers shoiuld not be put off. The beds were very comfortable and the jacuzzi bath was great, particularly after a long day of sight-seeing. Breakfast was not included in our deal but it is certainly worth the extra nine euros- the freshly squeezed orange juice is too good to be missed and the selection of hot and cold dishes is excellent. Location is perfect for getting around the Barri Gotic, El Raval, La Ribera etc and Placa Catalunya is only one hundred metres away. Staff were all amazingly helpful and polite- among the best I have ever encountered.

<Author>holl3411
<Content>Fantastic retreat Just returned from a thoroughly enjoyable 4 nights at the Hotel Montecarlo and wanted to echo the other positive reviews on this site. We booked the hotel direct via its website and found the prices better than a lot of those offered by generic agency websites.Arrived late on the Friday to a warm welcome and a complimentary bottle of Cava (for our anniversary). The room (Gracia/Superior) was great, with comfortable adjustable bed, luxurious marble bathroom with power shower and jacuzzi bath, separate lounge and entrance hall - All the facilities you would expect from a 4 star hotel with a lot of the touches you would associate with a 5 or above. (For example the proper hairdryer in the bathroom!)The hotel is very quiet both in terms of not seeing any other guests, but also being well sound proofed from the Rambla. It's a fantastic retreat from the noise and crowds of the street.One minor negative: on checking-in we were advised of building work taking place on the second floor (Pre-season stuff, only in the afternoons) and we were told that should there be any disturbance to call reception and they would move the builders onto another part of the building. Needless to say we were initially very sceptical and assumed the worse, however we didn't get disturbed whatsoever during our stay. (Having sampled the quality of service I have no doubts that the staff would indeed have moved the workers on!)

<Author>FAMILY44444
<Content>Yet another 5 star review for the Montecarlo! I booked this hotel based on the reviews and was not disappointed. I just looked over the last few dozen of those reviews and they're dead on.I was nevous given the picture on the hotel web site, but our rooms (512 and 513) were much nicer then the pictures.Location: On Las Ramblas and Portaferissa, about 100 yards south of Placa Catalunya (transport hub including 4 metro lines, airport bus and tourist buses) next to the Gothic quarter and 400 yards from the Cathedral.Room: stunningly modern; great cabinets, fixtures, bathrooms. The double glass doors DO eliminate the noise from the ramblas (though if a balcony is important to you, go with the 3rd or 4th floors the 5th floor has really just floor to ceiling sliding glass doors).we thougtht breakfast was stylish and worth experiencing; other days we got bread, cheese and ceral from the supermarket across the street.theres no coffee in the room and if you're morning people it could be hard to find a cup before 9 (and its that thick European coffee) I brought No-Doz. Theres a Burger King and a Mcdonalds at the top of the Ramblas.I don't know much about fine dining -- we ate prety cheap -- The Attic -- 20 yards south of the hotel -- was good with entres between 10 and 14 euros, and theres plenty of fast food on Las Ramblas. The Boqueria Market (70 yards south) has all sorts of fresh fruit and cheese and is also worth seeing as a tourist attraction. Fresc Co is a chain (6 of them in Barcelona) that has a salad/pizza/pasta bar. -- theres one near the Museo Picasso, one north of Placa Catalunya and one a block and a half west of the hotel.teenage girl shopping: the south eastern edge of Placa Catalunya, Porta d'angel (parallel to Las Ramblas, between Placa Catalunya and Portaferissa, and Portaferissa between Las Ramblas and Port d Angele mail me with questions: pcatalan@nycap.rr.comhave a ball!

<Author>eliledoll
<Content>Totally lived up to our expectations What an excellent hotel! - from the moment we arrived, the staff couldn't do enough for you. We were lucky enough to get a room with a balcony (ask for a high floor so you can get the best view of La Rambla and beyond) and it was luxuriously appointed with a Jacuzzi bath, adjustable beds, mini bar and a sound system. Towelling robes and slippers are also provided for guests comfort, and the bathrooms have hairdryers and a good range of complimentary toiletries.The sheets and towels are changed daily, and although the rate I got did not include breakfast my friend and I decided to treat ourselves;at 9 euros each it was plentiful, delicious and well worth the money.I was sceptical before arriving about the hotel's claim that the rooms were virtually soundproof - being that the hotel is situated on the busiest thoroughfare in Barcelona, but this is certainly the case.I would recommend that even if your room is not on the top floor you should take the lift to the 5th floor and walk up the short flight of stairs to the roof terrace - the views in all directions are stunning.I'm going back to the hotel next year with a larger group of friends,and although you can find cheaper accommodation in the city I feel its certainly worth the extra to stay at the Montecarlo.If you only have a short time to spend in City, I would thoroughly recommend you visit the Sagrada Familia - it's quite simply breathtaking. Also, on the far side of the Plaza de Catalunia is a street called the Passieg de Gracia - the shops are fabulous, and you can see two of Gaudi's famous landmark buildings ( La Pedrera and Casa Batllo). Enjoy!!

<Author>Whiskerskip
<Content>MonteCarlo quiet oasis on a busy street Date Oct 28, 2006We stayed only one night at the Hotel Montecarlo but would certainly be comfortable here for a week or longer. The staff is attentive, helpfull and polite. The rooms were quiet and clean. Even though the hotel is located directly on busy Las Rambles it is very quiet inside. There is an elevator to take you and your luggage to your floor.The Hotel is centrally located within walking distance to many areas of interest. The staff recommended Ciutat Condal located just North of Placa de Catalunya for an evening meal of tapas and it was a wonderful experience. There is a supermarket Carrefour located across the street from the hotel that is handy. Even though this was a short stay we would stay here again.

<Author>Elizabeth02445
<Content>Lovely hotel, great location, reputation well-deserved We just finished spending a week at the Hotel Montecarlo and loved every minute of it. Our room overlooked La Rambla, which meant that if we wanted to enjoy the street scene we could--but the double windows meant that we could also completely shut out the noise.Our room was comfortable, large enough, and spotless. The hotel breakfast can be skipped--but there are lots of cafes nearby and the Barcelona market is only 100 metres down the street and that's a great place to have coffee and a croissant--or even bacon and eggs. The location is great. It's close enough both to L'Eixample on the one hand and the waterfront on the other so that we were able to walk most of the places we wanted to see.The staff lived up to its reputation for being attentive. We arrived at the hotel without our luggage and they did everything they could--calling the airlines several times a day--to track it down and ensure that it arrived. We hope to be able to stay here again.

<Author>malousadiua
<Content>A big gem of a little hotel! My husband and I stayed at this hotel from 18-24th of Sept. 2006.We loved the positon of the hotel in Las Ramblas, right in the middle of the action!You could walk to the sights, great shopping at the Passeig de Gracia... a great place from where to explore the city.The hotel facade is so pretty that tourists frequently stop and take pictures, especially at night.The room itself was furnished very well. It was a mini suite, very roomy with a big, comfortable bathroom. It had a jacuzzi tub/shower and a bidet.All is great at this hotel but the greatest thing was our BED!!! It was the most comfortable, the best bed I have ever slept in all my life! That coming from a veritable Princess (as in Princess and the Pea!)This bed was to die for. It was one of those adjustable beds where you could lift the top of the bed, the bottom of the bed, and adjust it to everywhere in between. Each side of the bed is completely adjustable! Not only that, the mattress was not too hard, not too soft, it was just right!The sheets were just the right softness, not too starchy, and the pillows were incredible. I wanted to ship home the whole kit and caboodle! The sheets, the pillows, the adjustable bed, everything!I was ready to trade in my Tempurpedic bed at home to get this particular bed and sheets. I tried to figure out which manufacturer made the sheets but they were unmarked. I did buy the best sheets at El Corte Ingles but they were not as good.(I got to try them out at home later.)I couldn't wait to get into the gloriousness of this bed every night.It was unbelievably good. Needless to say, everything else about Barcelona followed ensuite.The best restaurants-La Barceloneta and Botafumiero.Don't waste your money on Jean Luc Figueras, that was a total waste of 200+ Euros. We couldn't get into Huffman at all.Remember to ask for the adjustable bed when you book!Look no further, this is the best moderately priced hotel in Barcelona!  
<Date>Oct 21, 2006

After thoroughly researching hotels in the area I decided to book with the Montecarlo, which based on reading other reviews, met my expectations. The hotel lobby was very nice, the room was small but clean and we had a great view of las rambla from our balcony. The location of the hotel was great since we were right in the center of the area, most of what we wanted to do and see was within walking distance. Generally the front desk staff were very helpful with suggestions for where to eat and go out etc. We never ate at the hotel since there were so many options so close by so I can't comment on the food there.The only dissapointment with the hotel was the Internet access which was limited-I was never able to open or send any emails from my hotmail account. Also remember to bring your own travel iron as the hotel does not have one.

<Author>2gaydads
<Content>Beautiful Hotel, Incredibly Helpful Staff You can read all about this hotel -- its comfortable rooms, great value, location -- and I completely agree. We stayed for 3 nights in early August and loved it. I can't wait to get back to Barcelona and I'll be staying at the Hotel Montecarlo again.But what the reviews don't quite capture is how thoroughly welcoming and helpful and warm the hotel staff is, day and night. After 2 nights at the hotel, we were off to the airport for our return home. At the gate to board our first flight, to London Heathrow, the flight information suddenly disappeared and we were told to reclaim our checked luggage and go back in line for another flight. Well, this turned out to be the morning of the London raid on terrorists. Our flight to London (and then home from there) was not going to happen. With two young children, we decided to leave the chaos of the airport and head back to the safe haven of this lovely hotel and its lovely staff.They were, again, welcoming and helpful and concerned for us. They put us in the same rooms, at the same deeply discounted rate we had booked through their website. They directed us to travel agents, and I was able to use their lobby computer for website searching for a flight home. In a very stressful time, in an unfamiliar city far from home, the people at Hotel Montecarlo made us feel that we had a safe place to be and there were people who cared.

<Author>maw8
<Content>Fabulous stay! Comfortable, close to the fun! After touring Spain for a week it was a wonderful treat to stay in such a comfortable, quiet, happening place. The beds were fabulous and so was the bedding! We had a room overlooking Las Ramblas which is a very noisy place. However, the double-paned, double doored sliding doors worked like a charm. We heard no noise coming off the street. Our room was very nicely appointed and the AC was perfect. The weather was over 100 degrees each day so we really needed the relief from the heat.The Front Desk clerks were always super friendly, available, and knowlegible about the places we wanted to visit. There was never a backup. They all spoke English very, very well.The plumbing was quiet and the amenities were definitely four star. They can't get a higher rating because there is no restaurant and no pool but, hey, I was so very, very comfortable and food was VERY available on Las Ramblas that those weren't issues for me.I'd highly recommend staying on Las Ramblas because it's such a happening place. Yes, I held my purse close to me at all times but I did that everywhere in Spain. I loved all the fun street performers at all hours of the day or night. It was the best show in town for just a few euros in tips!We ate at a WONDERFUL tapas place called La Lluna that is about a block away. It is open only for lunch but at about 12 euros a person it is not only a fabulous deal but the BEST meal we had in Spain. The hop-on-hop-off bus was disappointing. It was very, very hot on the top of the bus and the lines were so long you didn't really want to get off. I felt it didn't really go very close to anything but the Gaudi houses which is maybe 1/2 hour of the tour, the rest of the 1.5 hours of the drive on the red line is just driving up and down to drop people at the different stops that are a block or more away so you really couldn't take a peek while you were on the bus. I would say that it was worth doing but do it only for one day. Once the summer lines slow down it might be fine.Due to the location on this busy street the taxi drivers have to drop you off across from the hotel. It wasn't a problem for my friend and I since we only had one bag each. We didn't have to walk far at all. However, if you're traveling with more bags than you can carry yourself you might rethink staying here.I LOVED this hotel and would go back in a heartbeat.  
<Date>Aug 8, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel, horrible location First time to Barcelona for hubby and I. Liked the Hotel Monte Carlo - modern entrance, staff excellent, large rooms. However, I hated the location. La Rambla is filled with pickpockets, theives and gypsies...I hated being on that street. I noticed pickpockets stand outside the doors of the hotel and follow guests out...It was pretty scary. If you like safety, I would highly recommend a hotel on the Gran Via Passieg de la Gracia - the big street with all the expensive stores. My husband and I felt very safe dining and shopping there. No pickpockets in site! Besides the location, I found our washroom not to be cleaned well (hair all over the floor upon arrival!). I didn't like that at all. However, the rooms were large and the adjustable beds were amazing! I want to buy one for home now! So there were some pros and cons. Nice hotel, but next time, I would spend a bit more money to stay in a safer area. I guess it's personal preference...

<Author>funaway
<Content>Exceeded our expectations. I have to agree with all the positive reviews. From the time of our arrival until the end of our 3 night stay ( 06/14-06/17) in Barcelona could not find anything negative to say about the place. Fantanstic location near the top of La Rambla, near plaza Cataluniya (sorry for the spelling), probably the best location possible, for us. Great room with a little balcony facing La Rambla, more like a suite, really, with a foyer, small living area and a huge bathroom w/ jacuzzi. 4 sets of dual glazed aluminum sliding doors blocking all the noise, not 2 as many reviews stated. In-room safe, minibar, sweet wine and chocolates on our arrival. The room was basic but charming. Everything we needed steps away, including Starbucks. Barcelona is a gorgeous and safe city. Charm and atmosphere at least on par with places like Rome. No purse snatching or pickpocket incidents to report. Great restaurants which are reasonably priced. In smaller shops on La Rambla (basically a tourist center) always ask about the price before you buy, or chances are you will be overcharged. Agree on the price with taxi drivers before you get in. Our cab driver decided to overcharge us 10 euros on a way back to the airport. There were 4 euros on the meter when we got in, plus he wanted 7 euros surcharge for our 3 bags. About 10 euros more than what we paid on the way to the hotel. And no matter what, STAY AWAY from money exchange booths on La Rambla, especially the two which are located to the right of the hotel, on the same side of the street, on the way to Plaza Catalunya. The posted exchange rate in columns 1 and 2, already a little high, is misleading, since it only refers to sums of 6,000 euros or larger. Exchange rate for smaller sums is typically in small hard to see letters which refer to columns (typically 3, 4, or 5) with higher rates. In one of the places I mentioned the lady wanted to charge me 18% commission which she immediately agreed to reduce to 5%. I would not pay 5% and moved on to the one next door, a little closer to the hotel. In that exchange booth I pointed to the column which indicated $1.33 per euro and asked if that is the rate and if it included the commission. The lady at the counter said yes. The official exchange rate that day was $ 1.259 per 1 euro. But when I handed her $ 300 she exchanged it at $1.42 per 1 euro. After my immediate protests, she refused to return my $300 (she probably already spent $ 30 she ripped off from me in her mind), pointing to the column which indicated $ 1.58 per 1 euro, saying she gave me $1.42 rate instead of $ 1.58 as a favor. Small writing behind her (you couldn't even see it when she was sitting down) indicated that column to apply for exchanges under 6,000 euros. I decided not to get ripped off on principle and was able to get my money back with the help of 2 policemen which were passing by. The only reason I got my money back was that $ 1.42 per 1 euro rate did not appear in any column. The best rate I could get in Barcelona was $ 1.33 per 1 euro, including commission, from a bank. My worst experiences in exchanging currency were in Spain, particularly in Barcelona. Overall, the people are nice and there is plenty to see and do in that beautiful city.  
<Date>Jul 4, 2006

<Author>hermitcrabFrance
<Content>Montecarlo almost perfect We booked a saria room, and also requested a quiet room.W e were at the side/back and that was fine, wonderful shutters operated from the beds so kept us quiet and dark easily. The saria was a delight, a lovely little sitting area with a sound system so we bought a CD or two to relax too, great bathroom with jacuzzi bath, small dressing area with hanging space etc.And a decent size bedroom with twin beds that elevated at feet and head. This was perfect for my husband who has arthritic ankles, as was the position of the hotel, near everything. The breakfasts were somewhat expensive and disappointing, bad coffee and lack of fresh fruit, breads etc very good and freshly squeezed orange juice was terrific, so it should be in Spain!We sat and read in in the Grand Salon with its overdecorated 19th C style and Corbusier furniture, a pleasing contrast.The bar was neither here nor there, but we had a brandy on the house and good service at all times.The 2 day bus hop- on -and -hop- off ticket is good value and gives you the lie of the land for return individual trips, we didn't hop and off as the queues were very long, an hour for the first bus, because it was the May bank holiday.Ate at the Seven Doors near the harbour, Okish, at two or three local places in the Ramblas, very relaxing and one big treat at the Casa Calvi. Would definitely stay here again.

<Author>Chrisandlynne
<Content>Expecting too much? After reading all the eulogistic reviews of the Hotel Montecarlo, perhaps we were expecting a little too much of this good (but not fantastic) hotel. We came away a little deflated but well rested after a 3 night stay. Firstly, the positives - The frontdesk staff were attentive, helpful and knowledgable. The room was clean (but see other comments later), the towels and robes very comfortable and the jacuzzi bath good fun. The adjustable bed was very good for elevating the feet after a long walking day. The hotel's position halfway along La Rambla is perfect. Now the disappointments - The room (403) was very small with no dressing table nor mirror, except in the bathroom where it was regularly steamed up. Tea / coffee making facilities would have been nice also. The carpet was very badly marked and stained including several cigarette burns. The furniture was cheap, shoddy and likewise stained. Our window view was of a blank wall 10m away. We asked to be moved and offered to pay for an upgrade but the hotel was full. We paid 190 Euros for the room per night directly booked with the hotel. The bar was very basic, lacked comfort and atmosphere. It was rarely staffed so you had to interupt the frontdesk for service. Here I admit to being ultra-critical and this probably doesn't matter to most people. However, we like to have a relaxing glass of beer or wine at the end of the day and in the evenings.All in all it was a fairly pleasant place to stay (no better than that) and a deluxe room, rather than basic, is definately recommended.

<Content>Nice Hotel, but a few snags .... Nice location. Sorta like staying in Times Square, Catalan style.This is a nice hotel but with some MINOR problems.Had problems with misinformation about internet avilability (this was a business trip). Seems that not ALL rooms have internet (free or paid), and the solo terminal in the lobby has a misfunctional keyboard. Front desk was very enthusiatic if not always very efficient. Bell captain Jordie was verbally rude when forced by front desk to open the Grand Salon which had internet access.I realize most folks won't go here requiring business help (seemed a largely bewildered American cruise clientele) but just in case, be forewarned.We ordered a car through the front desk, two days before departure to go to the airport (thinking shuttle or private car), and got a taxi with 3.75 E already on the meter, and a taxi driver who had no brakes and used the handbrake all the way to the airport.When inquiring for a casual, reasonably priced local cuisine restaurant nearby, the restaurant recommended to us by the front desk QUO VADIS, wound up being very expensive and again, very American, with a vociferous patron demaning that the bar tender make him a Manhattan with lots of damned ice this time.The room was quiet, faced a wall and the beds were good. Walls are paper thin. Decor minimalist.We had fun in between work, strolling the Old Gothic section and enjoying great meals at Can Culleteras and Taller de Tapas; also enjoyed an expensive but once-in-a-lifetime night at the Opera within walking distance of the hotel... the real opera, not the Marx Brothers.No purse snatching incidents to report or witness.Go and have fun! This hotel is fine; just not quite grown-up yet.Maybe go for a pricier room to ensure amenities.PROS-Jacuzzi tubsEnglish speaking front deskGreat locationNice bathrobes and slippersVery clean, if a bit tired (carpet, drapes); maybe just our roomCONSPricey breakfastInternet Issues; don't count on itPoor dining recommendationsPoor front desk communications (we speak Spanish, also)Poor business and airport limo help.Cranky bell captain (who had been liberally tipped the day before)

<Author>jwb_ireland
<Content>Everything They Say Is True! Just back from a weekend break in Barcelona and we stayed 3 nights at the Montecarlo. We had a Gracia room on the 4th floor at a rate of 224 euro per night (not including breakfast).The hotel is in a fantastic location - right on Las Ramblas and just a quick walk from the centre of the action - Placa Catalunya. Las Ramblas is a just a continuous sea of people, traders, street entertainers and is, iniitally, a little overwhelming. But, step inside the door of Hotel Montecarlo and it's an oasis of calm and silence.The staff are all incredibly friendly and courteous - and they all speak perfect English. Honestly, I've only experienced a similar level of consistent service at a 5-star hotel.The room was huge - large enough sleeping area and a separate seating/lounge room. Two TVs! A CD/FM unit! A jacuzzi in the bathroom! Is this really a 3-star hotel??? Oh - free internet access from each room and an internet-enabled PC in the lobby!Yes...the crack between the 2 beds can be a little annoying but no big deal to be honest. Las Ramblas is a noisy, bustling street but, from the room, we couldn't hear a thing.If you are going to Barcelona - stay at this hotel! It's as good as all the other reviews say!

The hotel is every bit as excellent as people say it is, and the staff could not do enough for us when we arrived for a special occasion.
